the HTTP Server waits gracefully for existing requests to complete\\n50:       up to '60s' (dictated by ShutdownTimeout)\\n51: \\t- active long running requests will receive a GOAWAY.\\n52: \\n53: T0+70s: HTTPServerStoppedListening:\\n54: \\t- this event is signaled when the HTTP Server has stopped listening\\n55:       which is immediately after server.Shutdown has been invoked\\n56: \\n57: T0 + 70s + up-to 60s: InFlightRequestsDrained: existing in flight requests have been drained\\n58: \\t- long running requests are outside of this scope\\n59: \\t- up-to 60s: the default value of 'ShutdownTimeout' is 60s, this means that\\n60:       any request in flight has a hard timeout of 60s.\\n61: \\t- it's time to call 'Shutdown' on the audit events since all\\n62: \\t  in flight request(s) have drained.\\n63: \\n64: \\n65: The following is a sequence of shutdown events that we expect to see with\\n66:   'ShutdownSendRetryAfter' = true:\\n67: \\n68: T0: ShutdownInitiated: KILL signal received\\n69: \\t- /readyz starts returning red\\n70:     - run pre shutdown hooks\\n71: \\n72: T0+70s: AfterShutdownDelayDuration: shutdown delay duration has passed\\n73: \\t- the default value of 'ShutdownDelayDuration' is '70s'\\n74: \\t- the HTTP Server will continue to listen\\n75: \\t- the apiserver is not accepting new request(s)\\n76: \\t\\t- it includes new request(s) on a new or an existing TCP connection\\n77: \\t\\t- new request(s) arriving after this point are replied with a 429\\n78:       \\t  and the  response headers: 'Retry-After: 1` and 'Connection: close'\\n79: \\t- note: these new request(s) will not show up in audit logs\\n80: \\n81: T0 + 70s + up to 60s: InFlightRequestsDrained: existing in flight requests have been drained\\n82: \\t- long running requests are outside of this scope\\n83: \\t- up to 60s: the default value of 'ShutdownTimeout' is 60s, this means that\\n84:       any request in flight has a hard timeout of 60s.\\n85: \\t- server.Shutdown is called, the HTTP Server stops listening immediately\\n86:     - the HTTP Server waits gracefully for existing requests to complete\\n87:       up to '2s' (it's hard coded right now)\\n88: */\\n89: \\n90: // lifecycleSignal encapsulates a named apiserver event\\n91: type lifecycleSignal interface {\\n92: \\t// Signal signals the event, indicating that the event has occurred.\\n93: \\t// Signal is idempotent, once signaled the event stays signaled and\\n94: \\t// it immediately unblocks any goroutine waiting for this event.\\n95: \\tSignal()\\n96: \\n97: \\t// Signaled returns a channel that is closed when the underlying event\\n98: \\t// has been signaled. Successive calls to Signaled return the same value.\\n99: \\tSignaled() <-chan struct{}\\n100: \\n101: \\t// Name returns the name of the signal, useful for logging.\\n102: \\tName() string\\n103: }\\n104: \\n105: // lifecycleSignals provides an abstraction of the events that\\n106: // transpire during the lifecycle of the apiserver. This abstraction makes it easy\\n107: // for us to write unit tests that can verify expected graceful termination behavior.\\n108: //\\n109: // GenericAPIServer can use these to either:\\n110: //   - signal that a particular termination event has transpired\\n111: //   - wait for a designated termination event to transpire and do some action.\\n112: type lifecycleSignals struct {\\n113: \\t// ShutdownInitiated event is signaled when an apiserver shutdown has been initiated.\\n114: \\t// It is signaled when the `stopCh` provided by the main goroutine\\n115: \\t// receives a KILL signal and is closed as a consequence.\\n116: \\tShutdownInitiated lifecycleSignal\\n117: \\n118: \\t// AfterShutdownDelayDuration event is signaled as soon as ShutdownDelayDuration\\n119: \\t// has elapsed since the ShutdownInitiated event.\\n120: \\t// ShutdownDelayDuration allows the apiserver to delay shutdown for some time.\\n121: \\tAfterShutdownDelayDuration lifecycleSignal\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PreShutdownHooksStopped event is signaled when all registered\\n124: \\t// preshutdown hook(s) have finished running.\\n125: \\tPreShutdownHooksStopped lifecycleSignal\\n126: \\n127: \\t// NotAcceptingNewRequest event is signaled when the server is no\\n128: \\t// longer accepting any new request, from this point on any new\\n129: \\t// request will receive an error.\\n130: \\tNotAcceptingNewRequest lifecycleSignal\\n131: \\n132: \\t// InFlightRequestsDrained event is signaled when the existing requests\\n133: \\t// in flight have completed. This is used as signal to shut down the audit backends\\n134: \\tInFlightRequestsDrained lifecycleSignal\\n135: \\n136: \\t// HTTPServerStoppedListening termination event is signaled when the\\n137: \\t// HTTP Server has stopped listening to the underlying socket.\\n138: \\tHTTPServerStoppedListening lifecycleSignal\\n139: \\n140: \\t// HasBeenReady is signaled when the readyz endpoint succeeds for the first time.\\n141: \\tHasBeenReady lifecycleSignal\\n142: \\n143: \\t// MuxAndDiscoveryComplete is signaled when all known HTTP paths have been installed.\\n144: \\t// It exists primarily to avoid returning a 404 response when a resource actually exists but we haven't installed the path to a handler.\\n145: \\t// The actual logic is implemented by an APIServer using the generic server library.\\n146: \\tMuxAndDiscoveryComplete lifecycleSignal\\n147: }\\n148: \\n149: // ShuttingDown returns the lifecycle signal that is signaled when\\n150: // the server is not accepting any new requests.\\n151: // this is the lifecycle event that is exported to the request handler\\n152: // logic to indicate that the server is shutting down.\\n153: func (s lifecycleSignals) ShuttingDown() <-chan struct{} {\\n154: \\treturn s.NotAcceptingNewRequest.Signaled()\\n155: }\\n156: \\n157: // newLifecycleSignals returns an instance of lifecycleSignals interface to be used\\n158: // to scope\n83: \t- up to 60s: the default value of 'ShutdownTimeout' is 60s, this means that\n84:       any request in flight has a hard timeout of 60s.\n85: \t- server.Shutdown is called, the HTTP Server stops listening immediately\n86:     - the HTTP Server waits gracefully for existing requests to complete\n87:       up to '2s' (it's hard coded right now)\n88: */\n89: \n90: // lifecycleSignal encapsulates a named apiserver event\n91: type lifecycleSignal interface {\n92: \t// Signal signals the event, indicating that the event has occurred.\n93: \t// Signal is idempotent, once signaled the event stays signaled and\n94: \t// it immediately unblocks any goroutine waiting for this event.\n95: \tSignal()\n96: \n97: \t// Signaled returns a channel that is closed when the underlying event\n98: \t// has been signaled. Successive calls to Signaled return the same value.\n99: \tSignaled() <-chan struct{}\n100: \n101: \t// Name returns the name of the signal, useful for logging.\n102: \tName() string\n103: }\n104: \n105: // lifecycleSignals provides an abstraction of the events that\n106: // transpire during the lifecycle of the apiserver. This abstraction makes it easy\n107: // for us to write unit tests that can verify expected graceful termination behavior.\n108: //\n109: // GenericAPIServer can use these to either:\n110: //   - signal that a particular termination event has transpired\n111: //   - wait for a designated termination event to transpire and do some action.\n112: type lifecycleSignals struct {\n113: \t// ShutdownInitiated event is signaled when an apiserver shutdown has been initiated.\n114: \t// It is signaled when the `stopCh` provided by the main goroutine\n115: \t// receives a KILL signal and is closed as a consequence.\n116: \tShutdownInitiated lifecycleSignal\n117: \n118: \t// AfterShutdownDelayDuration event is signaled as soon as ShutdownDelayDuration\n119: \t// has elapsed since the ShutdownInitiated event.\n120: \t// ShutdownDelayDuration allows the apiserver to delay shutdown for some time.\n121: \tAfterShutdownDelayDuration lifecycleSignal\n122: \n123: \t// PreShutdownHooksStopped event is signaled when all registered\n124: \t// preshutdown hook(s) have finished running.\n125: \tPreShutdownHooksStopped lifecycleSignal\n126: \n127: \t// NotAcceptingNewRequest event is signaled when the server is no\n128: \t// longer accepting any new request, from this point on any new\n129: \t// request will receive an error.\n130: \tNotAcceptingNewRequest lifecycleSignal\n131: \n132: \t// InFlightRequestsDrained event is signaled when the existing requests\n133: \t// in flight have completed. This is used as signal to shut down the audit backends\n134: \tInFlightRequestsDrained lifecycleSignal\n135: \n136: \t// HTTPServerStoppedListening termination event is signaled when the\n137: \t// HTTP Server has stopped listening to the underlying socket.\n138: \tHTTPServerStoppedListening lifecycleSignal\n139: \n140: \t// HasBeenReady is signaled when the readyz endpoint succeeds for the first time.\n141: \tHasBeenReady lifecycleSignal\n142: \n143: \t// MuxAndDiscoveryComplete is signaled when all known HTTP paths have been installed.\n144: \t// It exists primarily to avoid returning a 404 response when a resource actually exists but we haven't installed the path to a handler.\n145: \t// The actual logic is implemented by an APIServer using the generic server library.\n146: \tMuxAndDiscoveryComplete lifecycleSignal\n147: }\n148: \n149: // ShuttingDown returns the lifecycle signal that is signaled when\n150: // the server is not accepting any new requests.\n151: // this is the lifecycle event that is exported to the request handler\n152: // logic to indicate that the server is shutting down.\n153: func (s lifecycleSignals) ShuttingDown() <-chan struct{} {\n154: \treturn s.NotAcceptingNewRequest.Signaled()\n155: }\n156: \n157: // newLifecycleSignals returns an instance of lifecycleSignals interface to be used\n158: // to coordinate lifecycle of the apiserver\n159: func newLifecycleSignals() lifecycleSignals {\n160: \treturn lifecycleSignals{\n161: \t\tShutdownInitiated:          newNamedChannelWrapper(\"ShutdownInitiated\"),\n162: \t\tAfterShutdownDelayDuration: newNamedChannelWrapper(\"AfterShutdownDelayDuration\"),\n163: \t\tPreShutdownHooksStopped:    newNamedChannelWrapper(\"PreShutdownHooksStopped\"),\n164: \t\tNotAcceptingNewRequest:     newNamedChannelWrapper(\"NotAcceptingNewRequest\"),\n165: \t\tInFlightRequestsDrained:    newNamedChannelWrapper(\"InFlightRequestsDrained\"),\n166: \t\tHTTPServerStoppedListening: newNamedChannelWrapper(\"HTTPServerStoppedListening\"),\n167: \t\tHasBeenReady:               newNamedChannelWrapper(\"HasBeenReady\"),\n168: \t\tMuxAndDiscoveryComplete:    newNamedChannelWrapper(\"MuxAndDiscoveryComplete\"),\n169: \t}\n170: }\n171: \n172: func newNamedChannelWrapper(name string) lifecycleSignal {\n173: \treturn &namedChannelWrapper{\n174: \t\tname: name,\n175: \t\tonce: sync.Once{},\n176: \t\tch:   make(chan struct{}),\n177: \t}\n178: }\n179: \n180: type namedChannelWrapper struct {\n181: \tname string\n182: \tonce sync.Once\n183: \tch   chan struct{}\n184: }\n185: \n186: func (e *namedChannelWrapper) Signal() {\n187: \te.once.Do(func() {\n188: \t\tclose(e.ch)\n189: \t})\n190: }\n191: \n192: func (e *namedChannelWrapper) Signaled() <-chan struct{} {\n193: \treturn e.ch\n194: }\n195: \n196: func (e *namedChannelWrapper) Name() string {\n197: \treturn e.name\n198: }\n199: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes@da663405beb487d66c27a0220ea4073305ae9077/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go"}}}
